<div id="review_40648605" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/40648605" />
    <a title="Arminzerella" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1769011-arminzerella"><img alt="Arminzerella" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1275503782p2/1769011.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/40648605?book_show_action=true">Dec 21, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arminzerella" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arminzerella" href="/user/show/1769011-arminzerella">Arminzerella</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1769011-arminzerella?shelf=adult-fiction">adult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1769011-arminzerella?shelf=borrowed-from-the-library">borrowed-from-the-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1769011-arminzerella?shelf=young-adult-fiction">young-adult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1769011-arminzerella?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1769011-arminzerella?shelf=2009-abe-lincoln-nominee">2009-abe-lincoln-nominee</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1769011-arminzerella?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer40648605&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer40648605" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15235535385574032524">Jennifer Government works for the Government in a world where everyone takes their last name from their employer or their school (Hack Nike works for Nike, and Billy NRA joins the National Rifle Association, and Hayley McDonald’s goes to a McDonald’s school). Jennifer is tipped off that there’s going to be a murder when Nike releases its new and hottest shoe, but she fails to catch the perpetrator and gets herself shot in the line of duty. Jennifer, however, is relentless in her pursuit of justi</span>
  <span id="freeText15235535385574032524" style="display:none">Jennifer Government works for the Government in a world where everyone takes their last name from their employer or their school (Hack Nike works for Nike, and Billy NRA joins the National Rifle Association, and Hayley McDonald’s goes to a McDonald’s school). Jennifer is tipped off that there’s going to be a murder when Nike releases its new and hottest shoe, but she fails to catch the perpetrator and gets herself shot in the line of duty. Jennifer, however, is relentless in her pursuit of justice. As soon as she gets funding (she has to apply directly to the parents of the girl who is murdered for the money for her investigation), she makes it her business to prove that Nike is behind the killings.<br /><br />As it happens, Nike is behind the killings. They hire the mostly clueless Hack Nike to do it, who only realizes later on what it is he’s gotten himself into. When he does realize, he goes to the police, who don’t handle things as you’d expect. They give him two options – he carries out the killings, but they eventually catch him, or they carry them out (a subcontract), and he pays them to do it. Hack goes for option B. Nike comes after Hack and they find out that the police gave the contract to the NRA. Meanwhile, Violet, Hack’s girlfriend manages to get them into more trouble when she kills one of the top Nike businessmen in self defense. Jennifer manages to get her man – John Nike – and stick him with the responsibility for the murders. His ruthlessness is nothing compared to her sense of justice, particularly when she’s already got bone to pick with him (he was once her lover, and is the father of her daughter). <br /><br />In this possible future greed and brand/corporate loyalty has turned everyone against one another and the only thing that matters is making a profit, and being on the winning side when the chips fall. This is particularly frightening because it’s only a few steps removed from how our society already operates. Just give corporations and big business a bit more power and they will control the world. It’s good to know, though, that there are still a few good people who are willing to work within this structure to bring the bad guys down when their heads get too big for their shoulders and they start thinking they’re invincible. Jennifer Government ends on a very satisfying “got what they deserved” note. This should appeal to readers who like dystopian fiction and imagining what the near future might be like. Lots of action and Jennifer’s investigation keep this moving along at a nice clip.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15235535385574032524" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_197571944" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/197571944" />
    <a title="Jenny Maloney" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/854965-jenny-maloney"><img alt="Jenny Maloney" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1426173938p2/854965.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/197571944?book_show_action=true">Aug 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenny Maloney" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenny Maloney" href="/user/show/854965-jenny-maloney">Jenny Maloney</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385507592" href="/book/show/828160.Jennifer_Government">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/854965-jenny-maloney?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/854965-jenny-maloney?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/854965-jenny-maloney?shelf=funny">funny</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/854965-jenny-maloney?shelf=dystopian-futures">dystopian-futures</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/854965-jenny-maloney?shelf=moral-dilemmas">moral-dilemmas</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/854965-jenny-maloney?shelf=government">government</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/854965-jenny-maloney?shelf=corporations">corporations</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer197571944" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10710043712609792055">If McDonalds ruled the world: it would look like this book. <br/><br/>Or, rather, if Nike owned the world.<br/><br/><b>The Low-Down Dirty:</b><br/>Welcome to the not-so-far-away future, where everyone is identified by the company they work for. Hence, our trigger-man (in every sense of the word, sort of) is Hack Nike. Hack Nike works for John Nike and John Nike. **<i>No, that wasn't a typo. There are two John Nikes in this book. One is prettier than the other.</i>** John Nike has decided that the greatest marketing scheme of all time</span>
  <span id="freeText10710043712609792055" style="display:none">If McDonalds ruled the world: it would look like this book. <br /><br />Or, rather, if Nike owned the world.<br /><br /><b>The Low-Down Dirty:</b><br />Welcome to the not-so-far-away future, where everyone is identified by the company they work for. Hence, our trigger-man (in every sense of the word, sort of) is Hack Nike. Hack Nike works for John Nike and John Nike. **<i>No, that wasn't a typo. There are two John Nikes in this book. One is prettier than the other.</i>** John Nike has decided that the greatest marketing scheme of all time includes shooting ten teenagers to make the new shoe, the Nike Mercury, that much cooler and desireable. The Johns ask Hack to handle it.<br /><br />But Hack's not very good at this and outsources to the Police, who in turn outsource to the NRA -- who kill fourteen teenagers instead. <br /><br />Now Hack is being hunted by the Government: Jennifer Government. <br /><br /><b>How it Works:</b><br />Barry has pulled off a fast-moving, sometimes confusing feat of how-not-to-run-the-world. Considering the world-wide scope of this story, it's amazing the characters come together as well as they do. <br /><br />You've got unemployed people (a.k.a. 'entrepeneurs') working on computer viruses to sell to the highest bidder. You've got a government that can't prosecute criminals unless the victims agree to pay for said prosecution. You've got ambitious corporate-ladder climbers that make the Enron assholes look like pansies. It's an exciting set-up for things to go wrong.<br /><br />The most interesting parts are the people who somehow grow a conscience out of this whole debacle, and there are a surprising amount of them, which bodes well for humanity. Just be prepared, as a reader to keep a mental list of the cast of characters because Barry doesn't slow down to let you catch up. If you lose a person, you're outta luck for a little while until you can get your bearings. <br /><br />~Jenny<br /><a href="http://www.placeforthestolen.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Place for the Stolen</a><br /><a href="http://www.undergroundwritingproject.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Under Ground Writing Project</a></span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/123699133?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christopher McKitterick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christopher McKitterick" href="/user/show/679976-christopher-mckitterick">Christopher McKitterick</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer123699133" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14961981302252592577">I really like this book, which is saying a lot because I read it expecting to be able to put it down in a hurry. A really vicious satire on modern global consumerism, sort of a SPACE MERCHANTS for the 21st century. <br/><br/>The story follows a handful of apparently random characters whose lives meet and part weirdly, in a world where everyone’s last name is the company they currently work for or the corporation running the school they currently attend. Jennifer Government is a Jennifer who works for the </span>
  <span id="freeText14961981302252592577" style="display:none">I really like this book, which is saying a lot because I read it expecting to be able to put it down in a hurry. A really vicious satire on modern global consumerism, sort of a SPACE MERCHANTS for the 21st century. <br /><br />The story follows a handful of apparently random characters whose lives meet and part weirdly, in a world where everyone’s last name is the company they currently work for or the corporation running the school they currently attend. Jennifer Government is a Jennifer who works for the decaying United States Federated Economic Blocs (which includes Australia, where most of the action takes place), with the UPS code for Malibu Barbie tattooed under one eye (the cover character), a remnant of her first career as an advertising exec. Three pages into the book, we’ve learned that the marketing higher-ups at Nike have produced a shoe that sells for $2500 a pair, except that to drive up consumer interest they haven’t sold any for six months, and now they’re going to dump 400,000 or them on the global market amid a carefully calibrated campaign, and then they’re going to kill a few of the people who buy them, so that the sneakers get street-cred. <br /><br />Okay, it sounds crazy, but it’s hilarious, and it just gets better. Strongly recommended. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14961981302252592577" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_503718673" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/503718673" />
    <a title="Alex" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7858793-alex"><img alt="Alex" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546468430p2/7858793.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/503718673?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alex" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alex" href="/user/show/7858793-alex">Alex</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7858793-alex?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer503718673" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11620464055104122599">I started this book once or twice, and decided to add it to this year's book challenge. I just now finished it, and I have thoughts about it.<br/><br/>I liked the way Barry used his characters to drive the story. It reminded me a little bit of <i>Big Trouble</i> (the movie. I haven't read the book). He starts with these seemingly disparate characters and then throws them all into a roiling pot of conspiracies, assassination and kidnapping. <br/><br/>I've often heard as a person having a "cinematic" writing style, but I th</span>
  <span id="freeText11620464055104122599" style="display:none">I started this book once or twice, and decided to add it to this year's book challenge. I just now finished it, and I have thoughts about it.<br /><br />I liked the way Barry used his characters to drive the story. It reminded me a little bit of <i>Big Trouble</i> (the movie. I haven't read the book). He starts with these seemingly disparate characters and then throws them all into a roiling pot of conspiracies, assassination and kidnapping. <br /><br />I've often heard as a person having a "cinematic" writing style, but I think this is the first time I've experienced that phenomenon first hand. I kept imagining this book as a movie (BTW, Jeremy Piven would be an excellent John Nike, and I kept picturing Anna Torv from <i>Fringe</i> as the eponymous Jennifer Government).<br /><br />From a satirical standpoint, I understood what Barry was trying to do by creating a world in which a person's last name was dictated by what company they worked for and everything (including schools, police, etc.) was privatized. However, I felt that it needed a bit more context--it was hard for me to visualize this freaky view of our future.<br /><br />I was ready to give up on this book several times throughout, but the ending was very satisfying, so I forgive it of its sins.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11620464055104122599" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1584256807" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1584256807" />
    <a title="Thom" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2945070-thom"><img alt="Thom" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1422135250p2/2945070.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1584256807?book_show_action=true">Mar 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thom" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thom" href="/user/show/2945070-thom">Thom</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781400030927" href="/book/show/331669.Jennifer_Government">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2945070-thom?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1584256807" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2156565839734123525">This story takes place in an alternate universe where corporations are way stronger than the government, which is essentially its own company. The characters lack a family name, using their employer instead. How various individuals named John Nike or Mike McDonalds aren't often confused is not explained.<br/><br/>Max Barry has created an interesting world, as least in the places he explored. The rest feels like a thin facade with no internal logic. The nonexistent character growth is barely overshadowed b</span>
  <span id="freeText2156565839734123525" style="display:none">This story takes place in an alternate universe where corporations are way stronger than the government, which is essentially its own company. The characters lack a family name, using their employer instead. How various individuals named John Nike or Mike McDonalds aren't often confused is not explained.<br /><br />Max Barry has created an interesting world, as least in the places he explored. The rest feels like a thin facade with no internal logic. The nonexistent character growth is barely overshadowed by the arbitrary changes to character motivations. And yet...<br /><br />The book has been quite successful, and reads fairly quickly. The author has created a web game loosely based on the book (at Nationstates.net). I also felt drawn to read to the conclusion - though I am now happy to put this book in my past. Perhaps <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16158596.Lexicon" title="Lexicon by Max Barry" rel="nofollow noopener">Lexicon</a> will be a better example of his writing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2156565839734123525" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_66481503" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/66481503" />
    <a title="Scott" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/97448-scott"><img alt="Scott" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1180057777p2/97448.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/66481503?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scott" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scott" href="/user/show/97448-scott">Scott</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer66481503" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13617184896280823996">Like much speculative fiction, the premise is better than the execution, but the premise isn't even that great. This might have seemed edgy at one time, but after having explored the extreme anti-corporate culture a bit in college — you know, the "Ad Busters" phase that many of us go through — it's more tired and played out than anything else.<br/><br/>Any number of anti-corporate narratives are more satisfying and feature people you can actually care about: Mirror's Edge or Jet-Set Radio Future to name a</span>
  <span id="freeText13617184896280823996" style="display:none">Like much speculative fiction, the premise is better than the execution, but the premise isn't even that great. This might have seemed edgy at one time, but after having explored the extreme anti-corporate culture a bit in college — you know, the "Ad Busters" phase that many of us go through — it's more tired and played out than anything else.<br /><br />Any number of anti-corporate narratives are more satisfying and feature people you can actually care about: Mirror's Edge or Jet-Set Radio Future to name a couple video games, or the film Michael Clayton. In contrast, Jennifer Government is populated by shells. I can actually hardly remember where the main protagonist ends up at the end, and I just finished reading the book less than four hours ago.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13617184896280823996" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_6919507'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6919507-company"><img alt="Company" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/book/111x148-bcc042a9c91a29c1d680899eff700a03.png" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('7Annn4F5ESMQm9SgHWhKanWCcMs8fiuHTgDyY8SfFvv8RGZ5q6ShAFzBxK3bbWYnvC2IElv26M6s1pGRiDsJog==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('d8cjAuHjCRQ7nOfkcPlpszM1D/vb2ZkGwQNeZB1OED5niqLkyz65N3fG9+m2/EX++pr3IrxRWk8j1T2WUeoPZw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>
